## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position (restoring force, possibly nonlinear) and time (likely an external driving force). The equation of motion combines nonlinear restoring forces with possible time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (harmonically driven SHO)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven cubic nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven with quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven asymmetric oscillator)
- Mixed nonlinearity driven: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (general polynomial restoring + drive)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Driven with sinusoidal: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (phase-shifted driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order Duffing)
- Position-time coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * sin(c2 * t) (parametric + restoring)
- Softening spring driven: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (factored Duffing + drive)
- Multi-frequency drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (two-frequency driving)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of the potential well, indicating symmetric oscillation about equilibrium
- Even-power terms (x²) in restoring force break symmetry, suggesting asymmetric potential wells
- Periodic driving forces appear as cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms additive to the restoring force
- Parametric excitation manifests as multiplicative coupling x*cos(c*t) rather than additive driving
- Negative coefficient on x (restoring) combined with positive coefficient on x³ indicates a hardening spring (Duffing type)
- Positive coefficient on x combined with negative on x³ indicates softening spring behavior leading to bounded motion
- Absence of velocity variable in acceleration expression suggests either undamped system or that damping effects are negligible
- Time appearing only inside trigonometric functions indicates periodic external forcing with no secular drift
